# AWS Essential Training for Architects

> Amazon Web Services (AWS) is one of the most widely used cloud platforms in the world, which explains why it’s the top pick for many organizations looking to scale and reduce costs by adopting a cloud infrastructure strategy. This course serves as a comprehensive reference for solutions architects working within an AWS environment. Join instructor Shyam Raj as he covers key concepts of the AWS Wel

> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949) | 4h 1m | Intermediate | 4K learners

>

>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aligning-solutions?u=76281980&t=5)** There is no better time to learn how to create scalable, secure, and cost-optimized solutions in the AWS cloud.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aligning-solutions?u=76281980&t=13)** In this course, you will learn strategies like automation and event-driven architecture that architects use to design high-performing solutions.

> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aligning-solutions?u=76281980&t=21)** After the course, you will be able to apply these principles to your solutions and enhance your career profile as a cloud architect.

>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/what-you-need-to-know?u=76281980&t=8)** To appreciate the topics discussed in this course, I recommend that you have a basic understanding of cloud computing concepts.

#### AWS Well-Architected Framework
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=0)** Before we begin this journey of architecting in the AWS cloud, it is important to talk about two things; the AWS well-architected framework and the AWS shared responsibility model.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=11)** Understanding these will significantly impact the solutions we deploy in the cloud.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=17)** In this video, we'll cover the first; the AWS well-architected framework.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=23)** It is a conceptual framework or in other words, a collection of design principles to build secure, resilient, and high-performing solutions in the AWS cloud.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=34)** It has six pillars; operational excellence, security, reliability, performance efficiency, cost optimization, and sustainability.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=45)** Think of it like an architect's blueprint for a sturdy and efficient building.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=50)** Carefully planning the materials and designing the structure ensures that the building can withstand various challenges and serve its purpose.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=58)** Similarly, the AWS well-architected framework provides guidance to build resilient and optimized solutions that deliver on expected business goals.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=68)** The first pillar; operational excellence, focuses on creating solutions aligned with best practices and delivering a great customer experience.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=78)** It recommends that you perform operations as code.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=81)** Just like how you define your applications as code, AWS has services that allow you to define your infrastructure, applications, and operations as code.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=91)** Doing so allows you to leverage automation and speed up deployment, limit the chances of human error, and creates consistent output each time.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=101)** Another key recommendation of this pillar is to anticipate failure by conducting tests and evaluating the effectiveness of response procedures and also to use managed services.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=114)** AWS has many services that are fully managed, allowing administrators to focus on managing their application or solution instead of the infrastructure.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=123)** The second pillar is security.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=126)** Here, the focus is on improving the security posture by protecting data and systems.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=132)** A key recommendation of this pillar is to implement a strong identity foundation.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=137)** You can do this by applying the principle of least privilege, enforcing separation of duties, and using a centralized identity management solution.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=146)** You should also protect data at rest and in transit by configuring the appropriate encryption and access control mechanisms.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=155)** Your solutions should also ensure traceability, meaning all actions should be monitored and captured by logging systems.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=162)** Additionally, you should also apply security at all layers such as infrastructure, application, network, and data.
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=171)** Also, be prepared for security incidents by having well-defined incident response procedures and running simulations.
>
> **[3:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=180)** The third pillar is reliability.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=182)** The focus of this pillar is to build solutions that perform their intended functions and recover quickly from failures.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=190)** The key recommendation of this pillar is to design your solutions such that they can automatically recover from failure.
>
> **[3:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=197)** This can be done by continuously monitoring key metrics of your application and using automation to recover from failure conditions.
>
> **[3:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=206)** AWS has tools like CloudWatch and EventBridge that you can use to monitor metrics and react to events of interest.
>
> **[3:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=214)** It is also important to test recovery procedures.
>
> **[3:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=218)** Doing so allows you to test how a workload fails and validate recovery procedures.
>
> **[3:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=224)** To improve reliability, AWS also recommends scaling horizontally instead of vertically.
>
> **[3:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=230)** This can be done by replacing large resources with multiple smaller resources.
>
> **[3:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=236)** For example, you can replace a single 8xlarge EC2 instance with four 2xlarge EC2 instances, eliminating the single point of failure.
>
> **[4:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=247)** The fourth pillar is performance efficiency.
>
> **[4:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=250)** The focus of this pillar is to streamline the allocation of IT and compute resources so they can maintain efficiency as demands change and technologies evolve.
>
> **[4:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=261)** A key recommendation of this pillar is to use serverless architectures.
>
> **[4:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=266)** With serverless architectures, you do not need to maintain servers for running code or hosting static websites.
>
> **[4:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=273)** This approach reduces operational burden and could lead to potential cost savings as resources are only used when needed.
>
> **[4:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=281)** Another key recommendation is to deploy globally.
>
> **[4:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=284)** Deploying your solutions in multiple regions will lower latency and improve customer experience.
>
> **[4:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=292)** The fifth pillar is cost optimization.
>
> **[4:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=295)** The focus of this pillar is to minimize costs and improve return on investment.
>
> **[5:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=301)** A key recommendation of this pillar is to adopt a consumption model.
>
> **[5:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=305)** This means paying only for the resources you consume.
>
> **[5:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=309)** Stopping resources when not needed and using services like autoscaling can result in significant cost savings.
>
> **[5:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=317)** It is also important to analyze expenditure.
>
> **[5:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=320)** Doing so allows you to identify where you're spending the most, identify areas for optimization, and measure your return on investment.
>
> **[5:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=329)** The sixth pillar is sustainability.
>
> **[5:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=332)** The focus of this pillar is to minimize the environmental impact of running your workloads in the cloud.
>
> **[5:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=338)** Generally, cloud providers have a lower carbon footprint because they invest in energy-efficient power and cooling technology, and because cloud resources are shared across multiple customers.
>
> **[5:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=350)** A key recommendation of this pillar is to maximize utilization.
>
> **[5:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=354)** This means appropriately sizing your workloads.
>
> **[5:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=357)** For example, two servers running at 30% utilization are less efficient than one server running at 60% due to the baseline power consumption per host.
>
> **[6:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=368)** Using managed services can also help maximize utilization.
>
> **[6:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=372)** For example, when using serverless technologies such as AWS Lambda, AWS shares the underlying resources across multiple customers and hence the impact of common components like power and networking is also shared across customers, resulting in efficient operation.
>
> **[6:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=390)** While we've only focused on the key recommendations of each of the six pillars, you can find many more in the AWS documentation.
>
> **[6:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=398)** I encourage you to review these regardless of where you are in your cloud journey.
>
> **[6:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-well-architected-framework?u=76281980&t=402)** Applying these principles will lead to better architecture and provide a strong foundation for the long-term success of your cloud deployments.

#### Shared responsibility model
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=0)** Understanding the AWS shared responsibility model is key to architecting secure solutions in the cloud.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=7)** It outlines who is responsible for which element of the cloud.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=11)** Here are some common questions that come up when adopting the cloud.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=15)** Who will manage the hardware powering the virtual services?
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=19)** Who is responsible for the software components?
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=22)** Who is responsible for the operating system configuration?
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=26)** Who will configure the network?
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=28)** Who is responsible for encryption and access control?
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=31)** The shared responsibility model helps answer these questions.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=36)** It outlines the shared responsibility of security and compliance between AWS and the customer.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=42)** First, let's understand at a high level how AWS is architected.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=47)** At the base, you have physical servers powering all the services.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=52)** AWS shares the capacity of these physical servers across multiple customers.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=58)** AWS does this using a software called hypervisor.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=61)** The hypervisor allocates and manages resources of the physical servers such as the CPU and memory, to virtual services provided by AWS.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=70)** The hypervisor and physical servers are not visible to the customer.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=76)** AWS is always responsible for operating and managing the physical infrastructure hosting the services, the host operating system, and the virtualization layer, which is the hypervisor.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=87)** This is always the case regardless of the service or service type.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=91)** Customer responsibility is determined by the AWS service type.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=96)** AWS offers services in different categories, such as infrastructure as a service or IaaS, and platform as a service or PaaS.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=106)** Let's look at the shared responsibility model for Amazon EC2, a service that allows you to launch virtual machines.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=114)** It falls in the IaaS category because the infrastructure is fully configurable according to your preferences.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=121)** AWS is responsible for the physical hardware and its global infrastructure, consisting of regions, availability zones, and edge locations where it hosts the physical hardware.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=132)** AWS is also responsible for the software used to manage the hardware, that is, the hypervisor.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=138)** The hypervisor manages compute, storage, database, and networking associated with the physical hardware.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=145)** This is commonly referred to as security of the cloud.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=149)** The customer is responsible for security in the cloud.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=153)** So customer responsibilities include server and client-side encryption and network traffic protection.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=159)** This is to protect data at rest and in transit.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=163)** The customer is also responsible for managing the guest operating system, running on the virtual machines and their network and firewall configuration.
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=171)** Managing the platform and any applications running on the instances and identity and access management is the customer's responsibility.
>
> **[2:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=179)** For example, the customer is responsible for patching the guest operating system and any software applications running on them.
>
> **[3:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=186)** Finally, regardless of the service type, managing data is always the customer's responsibility.
>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=193)** Now, let's look at the shared responsibility model for Relational Database Service, also known as RDS.
>
> **[3:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=199)** It falls in the PaaS or platform as a service category because AWS provisions the platform, in this case the database, you simply host your data in it.
>
> **[3:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=209)** For PaaS offerings, in addition to managing physical hardware and the associated software, AWS also manages the operating system, network, and firewall configuration of the assets on which the database is installed.
>
> **[3:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=223)** AWS also manages the platform and the application.
>
> **[3:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=227)** The customer is responsible for client-side encryption, identity and access management, and applying the necessary network and firewall configuration.
>
> **[3:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=236)** Again, managing the data is always the customer's responsibility.
>
> **[4:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=241)** Now, let's talk about a more abstracted service like S3.
>
> **[4:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=245)** Simple Storage Service or S3, is an object storage service from AWS.
>
> **[4:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=251)** It has an interface that customers can use to upload objects and has minimal configuration settings such as encryption, logging, access control, and a few others.
>
> **[4:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=261)** When using Amazon S3, the customer is only responsible for client-side encryption, identity and access management, and the data.
>
> **[4:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=270)** AWS manages the rest of the components.
>
> **[4:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=274)** As we've just seen, the split of responsibilities depends on the service or service type, but the following are always true.
>
> **[4:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=282)** AWS is always responsible for the physical infrastructure and the hypervisor.
>
> **[4:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=287)** The customer is always responsible for managing data.
>
> **[4:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=291)** The customer is always responsible for managing identities and access, for example, user accounts and their permissions.
>
> **[4:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=299)** As you can see, the shared responsibility model clearly differentiates the responsibilities of AWS and the customer and establishes a framework based on shared commitment.
>
> **[5:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/shared-responsibility-model?u=76281980&t=309)** Understanding this will enhance your security posture and allow you to use AWS services confidently.

### 1. Keeping Things Secure

> [[#Table of Contents|↑ Back to Table of Contents]]

#### Design a strategy for secure access
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=0)** When architecting solutions in the cloud, one of the most important aspects to take care of is security.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=7)** Doing so allows you to take advantage of cloud technologies while protecting your data and systems.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=13)** The following design principles should be adhered to when architecting in the cloud.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=18)** First, it is important to implement strong identity and access management.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=24)** Consider how you will manage identities for your users and their access permissions.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=29)** You can manage identities within AWS or use an external identity provider.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=35)** Also, consider how you will securely grant access to external users who may need to access your resources and applications.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=44)** When granting access, the best practice recommendation is to implement the principle of least privilege.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=50)** This means granting only the minimum permissions required for the task or job role.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=56)** AWS has different policy types that you can use to grant and control access.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=61)** Identity-based policies allow you to define permissions for identities such as users and groups.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=68)** Resource-based policies allow you to define who has access to a resource and what actions can they perform on it.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=76)** Service control policies or SCPs, allow you to define the maximum permissions for member accounts in an AWS organization.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=86)** Next, secure every layer.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=89)** This includes the network, applications, code, data, instances such as EC2 instances and databases, and the operating system.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=100)** AWS has tools that allow you to secure these resource types and review their security.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=106)** We'll cover many of these in this section of the course.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=110)** Then protect data.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=112)** This is of prime importance because protecting data is key to maintaining customer confidence and complying with regulations.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=120)** Data protection begins with identifying and classifying data.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=124)** It is important to understand these key considerations.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=128)** Does the data contain personally identifiable information or PII such as name, address, date of birth, and more?
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=137)** Does it contain intellectual property such as secrets and patents?
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=142)** Does it contain protected health information such as medical records?
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=146)** Does it contain financial information such as credit card details?
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=151)** Where is the data stored?
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=153)** Who owns the data?
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=155)** Who can access and modify data?
>
> **[2:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=158)** What is the business impact if data is modified, deleted, or inadvertently disclosed?
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=164)** Answering these questions will help you determine the controls to implement to mitigate the risk.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=170)** These include authentication, encryption, access control, and reporting.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=176)** Also, it is important to protect data at rest and in transit.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=182)** You can protect data at rest by encrypting it and data in transit by using secure protocols such as HTTPS.
>
> **[3:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=189)** We'll talk more about these later in this section.
>
> **[3:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=194)** Next, implement traceability.
>
> **[3:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=196)** Traceability refers to the ability to track and monitor interactions and changes in your AWS environment.
>
> **[3:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=203)** Ensure you have tools and systems to monitor, alert, and audit actions and changes in real time.
>
> **[3:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=210)** You can use AWS-provided tools or tools available in the AWS marketplace to implement traceability.
>
> **[3:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=217)** For example, AWS CloudTrail allows you to maintain an audit trail of actions by users and services.
>
> **[3:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=225)** AWS Config allows you to record, audit, and evaluate the configuration of your AWS resources.
>
> **[3:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=232)** AWS X-Ray allows you to get an end-to-end view of requests as they travel through your application, allowing you to identify the root cause of performance issues and errors.
>
> **[4:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=242)** You can use VPC Flow Logs to capture information about IP traffic going to and from network interfaces in your VPC.
>
> **[4:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=251)** Tag resources to label them and assign ownership.
>
> **[4:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=256)** In addition to CloudTrail, you can also store logs in an Amazon S3 bucket or a CloudWatch log group for further analysis.
>
> **[4:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=265)** Lastly, prepare for security events.
>
> **[4:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=268)** Create and regularly update an incident response plan specific to your AWS environment.
>
> **[4:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=275)** Your plan will define the ability of your team to respond to an incident, restore operations, and perform forensic analysis.
>
> **[4:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=283)** To learn more about how you can create an incident response plan, I recommend reading the AWS documentation on this topic.
>
> **[4:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=290)** So those are the high points to bear in mind as you architect the security of your applications and workloads.
>
> **[4:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/design-a-strategy-for-secure-access?u=76281980&t=297)** Now, let's get to the details.

#### Identity and Access Management
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=0)** AWS IAM, or Identity and Access Management is a service that allows you to manage access to your AWS resources.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=8)** This includes access for internal and external users.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=13)** IAM is important from a solution architecture perspective because it allows you to design secure access for your resources.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=20)** Important entities in IAM include users, groups, policies, and roles.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=28)** A user in AWS consists of a name and credentials, and is usually associated with a human user.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=35)** You can group users to form user groups.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=39)** This approach simplifies access management by assigning permissions to groups instead of assigning them to individual users.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=48)** IAM also allows you to manage identities outside of AWS.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=52)** If you already have your user identities configured in an external identity provider, you can use these with AWS.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=60)** By doing so, you do not need to create IAM users in your AWS account.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=65)** This can be an important architectural decision, as this will determine whether AWS or an external identity provider manages your identities.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=74)** Microsoft Active Directory is a common identity provider used by customers.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=80)** You can use identity providers that support OpenID Connect, also known as OIDC or Security Assertion Markup Language 2.0, also known as SAML.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=91)** The next IAM entity is an IAM policy.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=96)** A policy is a document that contains permissions.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=99)** When associated with an identity or resource, it defines their permissions.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=105)** For example, here is a policy that grants read permissions to S3 buckets.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=110)** When this is assigned to a user, they will have get, list, and describe permissions on S3 buckets.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=118)** When multiple policies are associated with a user, the resulting access is the cumulative effect of the policies.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=126)** The next item entity is an IAM role.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=130)** It is similar to an IAM user in that it is an identity with permissions.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=135)** However, it is not uniquely associated with the user.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=138)** Instead, it is intended to be assumed by anyone who needs it.
>
> **[2:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=143)** Roles have policies associated with them that determine their permissions.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=149)** Imagine you have an EC2 instance that needs access to an S3 bucket.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=155)** AWS does not permit this access by default even if it is within your account.
>
> **[2:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=160)** By attaching an IAM role with appropriate permissions to the EC2 instance, you can grant it access to the bucket.
>
> **[2:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=168)** Here is another example.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=170)** Let's say you have a Lambda function that needs to send notifications by publishing to an SNS topic.
>
> **[2:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=177)** SNS is the notification service from AWS.
>
> **[3:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=181)** By default, the Lambda function won't be able to access the topic.
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=185)** By attaching an IAM role to the Lambda function, you can grant it the necessary permissions to publish to the topic.
>
> **[3:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=192)** You can also use IAM roles to grant access to other AWS accounts belonging to third parties to perform actions in your account.
>
> **[3:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=201)** For example, you may want to grant access to a third party to upload objects to an S3 bucket in your account or you may want to share your logs with a third party for monitoring and analysis.
>
> **[3:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=214)** Let's see how to do this.
>
> **[3:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=216)** Let's say we need to grant access to a trusted third party to read information about our EC2 instances.
>
> **[3:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=225)** Log in to the management console of the AWS account that will grant access to the trusted third party.
>
> **[3:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=232)** Use the services menu at the top then go to Security, Identity, and Compliance and then go to the IAM service.
>
> **[4:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=242)** Once you are here, click "Roles" on the left navigation pane and then click "Create role."
>
> **[4:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=249)** Here, you can set the trusted entity type as an AWS account.
>
> **[4:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=254)** Scroll down and select another AWS account and provide the AWS account ID of the trusted third party.
>
> **[4:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=262)** For enhanced security, AWS recommends using a random string as the external ID.
>
> **[4:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=268)** The third party must provide this external ID when assuming the role.
>
> **[4:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=272)** For now, we'll skip this.
>
> **[4:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=275)** You can also enforce that the third party use MFA or multi-factor authentication when assuming the role.
>
> **[4:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=282)** For now, we'll skip this and click "Next."
>
> **[4:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=285)** In the next step, you can add policies to grant permissions to the third party.
>
> **[4:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=291)** I'm going to search for the policy named EC2ReadOnlyAccess.
>
> **[4:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=296)** This is a preconfigured policy that grants read permissions to the EC2 service.
>
> **[5:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=302)** Select the policy and click 'Next."
>
> **[5:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=306)** Here, you can provide a name for the role.
>
> **[5:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=309)** I'm going to call this as EC2ReadOnlyAccess.
>
> **[5:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=314)** Review the configuration and click "Create role."
>
> **[5:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=321)** The role has been created, and here is the ARN or the unique identifier for the role.
>
> **[5:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=328)** Before a user can assume this role, it needs a few changes.
>
> **[5:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=332)** Scroll down and under the "Trust Relationships" tab, you will find the trust policy of this role.
>
> **[5:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=339)** It states that the assume role action is allowed for the root user of the trusted account.
>
> **[5:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=345)** However, the role will be used by an IAM user of the trusted account not the root user.
>
> **[5:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=351)** So we'll need to change this.
>
> **[5:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=353)** Click "Edit trust policy" and replace the root with user followed by the user name of the IAM user in the trusted account.
>
> **[6:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=362)** Scroll down and click "Update policy."
>
> **[6:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=366)** This AWS account, that is the trusting account, is now fully configured.
>
> **[6:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=371)** Let's now switch to the trusted account and see how to assume this role.
>
> **[6:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=376)** Here in another browser tab, I'm logged in as the root user on the trusted account.
>
> **[6:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=383)** IAM users who need to assume the role should be given the necessary permissions to perform the action.
>
> **[6:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=388)** In other words, they need the assumed role permission.
>
> **[6:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=392)** For this purpose, we'll need to create a new IAM policy that includes this permission.
>
> **[6:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=398)** So on the trusted account, use the services dropdown menu, go to security, identity and compliance and then go to the IAM service.
>
> **[6:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=408)** On the left navigation pane, click "Policies" and then click "Create policy."
>
> **[6:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=415)** From the services dropdown, select the STS service, also known as the Security Token Service.
>
> **[7:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=423)** It provides temporary access to trusted users.
>
> **[7:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=427)** Under the right section, you will find the assume role action.
>
> **[7:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=431)** You can assign this permission to the specific IAM role created in the trusting account by adding the role ARN here.
>
> **[7:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=439)** Or you can allow this permission to all resources allowing the user to assume any role.
>
> **[7:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=445)** We'll keep it simple and set it to all.
>
> **[7:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=449)** Click "Next" and provide a name for the policy then scroll down and click "Create policy."
>
> **[7:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=460)** The policy has been created and it should now be assigned to the IAM user, so they have the necessary permissions to assume roles.
>
> **[7:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=469)** On the left navigation pane, click "Users" and then click on the desired username.
>
> **[7:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=475)** Under the permissions tab, click "Add permissions" then select the option to attach policies directly and search for the policy you just created.
>
> **[8:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=487)** Select the policy, click "Next", review your selections and then click "Add permissions."
>
> **[8:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=496)** Now, we have the required configuration to allow the IAM user to assume the role.
>
> **[8:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=501)** Let's test it. On another browser tab, I'm logged in as the IAM user.
>
> **[8:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=508)** To assume a role, click your username in the top right-hand corner.
>
> **[8:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=513)** Here, you will find the "Switch role" button.
>
> **[8:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=516)** This option is only available when you are signed in as an IAM user.
>
> **[8:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=521)** Root users do not see this option.
>
> **[8:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=524)** Click "Switch role" and provide the account ID and the role name that you would like to assume.
>
> **[8:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=531)** I'll go back to the browser tab where I'm logged in as the trusting AWS account.
>
> **[8:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=536)** From here, I'll copy the AWS account ID and go back to this browser tab.
>
> **[9:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=541)** I'll provide the account ID and the name of the role that I'd like to assume then I'll click "'Switch role."
>
> **[9:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=552)** Now, I've switched or assumed the role.
>
> **[9:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=556)** The role and account information is shown on the top right-hand corner.
>
> **[9:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=560)** When I go to the EC2 service, I can view resources from the trusting account.
>
> **[9:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=566)** As you can see, using IAM roles to grant access to third parties is more secure than sharing account credentials.
>
> **[9:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/identity-and-access-management?u=76281980&t=574)** Also, having a clear strategy for managing identities is important to the security of your AWS environment.

#### Organizing multiple accounts with AWS Organizations
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/organizing-multiple-accounts-with-aws-organizations?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/organizing-multiple-accounts-with-aws-organizations?u=76281980&t=0)** It is common for organizations to have multiple AWS accounts.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/organizing-multiple-accounts-with-aws-organizations?u=76281980&t=4)** This may be for segregation of environments, regulatory compliance, creating security boundaries, and even to work around service limits imposed by AWS.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/organizing-multiple-accounts-with-aws-organizations?u=76281980&t=15)** For example, an organization may have separate AWS accounts for each business location, each department, and even for each project.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/organizing-multiple-accounts-with-aws-organizations?u=76281980&t=25)** It is common for organizations to have hundreds of AWS accounts.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/organizing-multiple-accounts-with-aws-organizations?u=76281980&t=30)** This creates administrative and architectural challenges such as identity and access management, cost management, cross-account resource access, and governance and compliance.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/organizing-multiple-accounts-with-aws-organizations?u=76281980&t=42)** AWS has several services to manage challenges associated with multiple AWS accounts.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/organizing-multiple-accounts-with-aws-organizations?u=76281980&t=48)** The most commonly used ones are AWS Organizations and AWS Control Tower.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/organizing-multiple-accounts-with-aws-organizations?u=76281980&t=53)** In this video, we'll talk about AWS Organizations and about AWS Control Tower in the next.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/organizing-multiple-accounts-with-aws-organizations?u=76281980&t=60)** AWS Organizations allows you to consolidate multiple AWS accounts into an organization that you can create and manage centrally.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/organizing-multiple-accounts-with-aws-organizations?u=76281980&t=70)** With AWS Organizations, you can invite other AWS accounts to join your organization and manage them centrally.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/organizing-multiple-accounts-with-aws-organizations?u=76281980&t=78)** You can consolidate billing at the management account to pay for all member accounts.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/organizing-multiple-accounts-with-aws-organizations?u=76281980&t=83)** You can group accounts into organizational units or OUs.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/organizing-multiple-accounts-with-aws-organizations?u=76281980&t=88)** You can use service control policies or SCPs to define the maximum permissions for member accounts in the organization.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/organizing-multiple-accounts-with-aws-organizations?u=76281980&t=97)** As you can see, architecting your AWS accounts to be centrally managed using AWS Organizations can simplify their management.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/organizing-multiple-accounts-with-aws-organizations?u=76281980&t=105)** Now, let's go to the AWS Management Console and see how to configure AWS Organizations.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/organizing-multiple-accounts-with-aws-organizations?u=76281980&t=112)** Login as the root user of an account that you intend to use as the management account of the organization.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/organizing-multiple-accounts-with-aws-organizations?u=76281980&t=119)** Use the services dropdown menu at the top.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/organizing-multiple-accounts-with-aws-organizations?u=76281980&t=122)** Go to management and governance and then go to AWS Organizations.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/organizing-multiple-accounts-with-aws-organizations?u=76281980&t=128)** Once you're here, click "Create an organization."
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/organizing-multiple-accounts-with-aws-organizations?u=76281980&t=132)** Doing so creates an hierarchy with the root organization unit at the top, and the current account is now the management account of the organization.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/organizing-multiple-accounts-with-aws-organizations?u=76281980&t=142)** Now, let's add another AWS account as a member account to this organization.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/organizing-multiple-accounts-with-aws-organizations?u=76281980&t=148)** Click "Add an AWS account."
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/organizing-multiple-accounts-with-aws-organizations?u=76281980&t=150)** You can create a new AWS account and add it to the organization or invite an existing account.
>
> **[2:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/organizing-multiple-accounts-with-aws-organizations?u=76281980&t=157)** Enter the email address or the account ID of the account you're inviting.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/organizing-multiple-accounts-with-aws-organizations?u=76281980&t=163)** Optionally add a message and click "Send invitation."
>
> **[2:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/organizing-multiple-accounts-with-aws-organizations?u=76281980&t=169)** Now the invited accounts owner will receive an invitation email with an option to accept and join the organization.
>
> **[2:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/organizing-multiple-accounts-with-aws-organizations?u=76281980&t=177)** Alternatively, you will also find the invitation in the management console of the invited account.
>

>

> **[3:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/organizing-multiple-accounts-with-aws-organizations?u=76281980&t=204)** Now, this account has joined as a member account of this organization.

> **[3:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/organizing-multiple-accounts-with-aws-organizations?u=76281980&t=211)** Back over here, I'll refresh the page.

>
> **[3:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/organizing-multiple-accounts-with-aws-organizations?u=76281980&t=225)** Let's further explore AWS Organizations.
>
