Under trust relationships, the EventBridge scheduler is allowed to assume this role.
>
> **[7:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/event-driven-architecture?u=76281980&t=478)** AWS has a document that explains how to create a service role for EventBridge.
>
> **[8:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/event-driven-architecture?u=76281980&t=483)** Back over here to the EventBridge Console, let's go to the next step.
>
> **[8:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/event-driven-architecture?u=76281980&t=487)** This is the last step where you can review your selections and create the schedule.
>
> **[8:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/event-driven-architecture?u=76281980&t=493)** Now, the schedule will start the instance at the configured time.
>
> **[8:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/event-driven-architecture?u=76281980&t=497)** Similarly, we can create another rule to invoke the stop EC2 instance action.
>
> **[8:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/event-driven-architecture?u=76281980&t=503)** So as we've just seen, you can use EventBridge to react to events in real time and architect event-driven, loosely coupled solutions.
>
> **[8:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/event-driven-architecture?u=76281980&t=511)** The possibilities are immense.
>
> **[8:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/event-driven-architecture?u=76281980&t=513)** We've only scratched the surface here, and I encourage you to incorporate EventBridge in your applications.

#### Orchestrating with Step Functions
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=0)** Orchestration is a common challenge when using automation in your solutions.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=4)** Orchestration refers to coordinating and managing interconnected tasks to accomplish a specific workflow.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=11)** Consider the example of a data processing pipeline.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=15)** It involves multiple steps such as data ingestion, validation, transformation, and storage.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=21)** Each step requires the use of different AWS services and coordination between them.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=26)** When orchestrating a solution like this, you may find these challenges: Sequential execution where the solution requires the output of one step to become the input of the next step.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=37)** Parallel execution, where the solution may need to execute certain steps concurrently to improve performance.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=44)** Error handling, where each step may encounter issues that need to be handled and may even need a retry logic.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=50)** Some steps may have timeouts and need to be resumed.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=54)** And lastly, visibility into the execution of each step to monitor the progress of the pipeline.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=60)** AWS Step Functions helps address these challenges.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=64)** It is a serverless orchestration service.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=67)** It allows you to coordinate the components of distributed applications and microservices using visual workflows.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=75)** It has a graphical console that allows you to see your applications workflow as a series of event-driven steps.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=82)** Here are some use cases that you can address with Step Functions.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=86)** Function orchestration; a workflow that runs a group of steps in a specific order.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=91)** Branching; a workflow that makes a decision based on the input.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=96)** Error handling; where you use a retry statement to handle unsuccessful requests.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=101)** Human in the loop; where you pause a workflow until a human approval is obtained.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=107)** Parallel processing; where you have separate branches that execute concurrently and wait until all branches terminate before going to the next task.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=116)** And dynamic parallelism; where you run a set of workflow steps for each item in a data set.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=122)** The iterations run in parallel, making it possible to process data sets quickly.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=128)** In Step Functions, a workflow is called a state machine, which is a series of event-driven steps.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=135)** Each step in the workflow is called a state.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=138)** States can perform a task, choose between branches of execution, stop an execution with a failure or success, begin parallel branches of execution, dynamically iterate steps, or provide a delay for a certain amount of time.
>
> **[2:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=154)** Now, let's go to the AWS Management Console and see how to create a state machine.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=161)** I'm here at the AWS Management Console.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=164)** You will find Step Functions under the "Application Integration" section.
>
> **[2:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=169)** Let's create a new state machine for an e-commerce workflow.
>
> **[2:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=174)** The workflow starts when a customer has attempted payment to purchase an item.

> **[2:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=179)** Here, you have pre-configured templates.

>
> **[3:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=221)** You will find it under the flow tab.
>
> **[3:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=223)** Note that you have other flow states such as parallel, map, weight, and others.
>
> **[3:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=229)** I'll drag a choice state and drop it under the Lambda invoke action.
>
> **[3:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=233)** We'll use the left branch for successful payments and the right branch for failed payments.
>
> **[3:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=239)** If payment has failed, we'll send an email to the customer with a retry link.
>
> **[4:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=244)** For this purpose, we'll use an SNS publish action state.

>
> **[4:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=253)** I'll name it as send failed email with retry link.
>
> **[4:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=258)** If payment is successful, we want to update the inventory which is maintained in a DynamoDB database.
>

>
> **[4:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=271)** I'll name it as Update Inventory.

>
> **[5:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=303)** I'll name this as Send Success email with invoice.
>
> **[5:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=309)** Finally, we'll add the success date to the left branch to mark the workflow as success.
>
> **[5:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=315)** Similarly, we'll add the failed state to the right branch to mark that workflow as a failure.
>
> **[5:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/orchestrating-with-step-functions?u=76281980&t=322)** So that's our state machine.

#### AWS Systems Manager
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=0)** Now, let's talk about a popular AWS service known as Systems Manager.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=5)** AWS Systems Manager allows you to centrally view and manage resources in AWS and multi-cloud hybrid environments.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=13)** It has many features which are broadly classified under application management, change management, node management, and operations management.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=22)** Application management helps DevOps engineers investigate and remediate issues with their resources in the context of their applications.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=31)** Change management allows you to request, approve, implement, and report on operational changes to your application configuration and infrastructure.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=40)** Node management allows you to manage configured instances, also known as nodes.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=44)** With node management, you can manage compliance, software inventory, patches, and configuration of your instances.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=52)** Operations management allows you to manage incidents and use dashboards to view your resources.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=58)** Systems manager has many capabilities that make it an important tool for managing your assets.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=64)** In this video, we'll specifically focus on the automation capability of Systems Manager.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=69)** It allows you to perform common maintenance, deployment, and remediation tasks.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=74)** Automation uses runbooks.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=76)** A runbook is a set of pre-configured instructions to perform a task.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=81)** Here is a runbook that disables public read and write access on an S3 bucket.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=87)** It has the S3 bucket name and an IAM role to be assumed as its parameters.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=93)** It then executes an API to make the configuration change.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=97)** The API action has the API detail, bucket name, and attributes to be modified.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=104)** AWS provides many pre-configured runbooks.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=108)** For example, you have preconfigured runbooks to archive EBS snapshots, disable public access for security groups, enable S3 bucket encryption, set required tags, and several more.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=121)** You can also create custom runbooks.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=124)** Systems Manager automation allows you to run automations on a fleet of AWS resources.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=130)** You can target resources for automation by using tags, resource groups, and parameter values.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=136)** You can run Systems Manager automations across multiple AWS regions.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=141)** You can also run on multiple AWS accounts or AWS organization units from a central account.
>
> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=147)** Doing so reduces the time required to administer your AWS resources.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=152)** You can also start an automation by specifying a runbook as the target of an Amazon EventBridge event.
>
> **[2:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=158)** You can also start automations according to a schedule.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=161)** When running automations on a fleet, you can rate control by setting a concurrency value and an error threshold.
>
> **[2:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=168)** The concurrency value determines how many resources are allowed to run the automation simultaneously.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=175)** The error threshold determines how many automations can fail before Systems Manager stop sending the automation to other resources.
>
> **[3:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=183)** Now, let's go to the AWS Management Console and see a quick example of how to use the automation feature of Systems Manager.
>
> **[3:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=191)** Once you're at the Management Console, you will find Systems Manager under the "Management and Governance" section.
>
> **[3:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=201)** From here, you will find the different functions we talked about, such as operations, application, change, and node management.
>
> **[3:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=210)** Let's go to automation which is under change management.
>
> **[3:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=214)** Let's execute an automation.
>
> **[3:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=217)** Here, you will find runbooks provided by AWS.
>
> **[3:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=220)** There are plenty of them and they are broken down into different categories such as remediation, patching, security, and others.
>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=228)** Let's execute a runbook that will enable versioning on S3 buckets.
>
> **[3:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=233)** Versioning allows you to keep multiple versions of a file and restore deleted versions.
>
> **[3:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=239)** This runbook is on Page 2.
>
> **[4:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=241)** Clicking on the runbook will open it in a new browser tab.
>
> **[4:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=246)** Here, we have details like what the document does and input and output parameters.
>
> **[4:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=252)** Scroll down to find a graphical representation of the actions performed by the runbook.
>
> **[4:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=257)** Now, let's execute this.
>
> **[4:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=260)** You can perform a simple execution or a rate control execution, which is a good option when executing at scale, or execute in multiple accounts and regions, or perform a manual execution.
>
> **[4:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=273)** Let's use the rate control option, which will allow us to execute on multiple targets.
>
> **[4:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=278)** Scrolling down, you will find the target section where you can define the parameter to include in the runbook.
>
> **[4:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=285)** This depends on the runbook you're using.
>
> **[4:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=287)** For this execution, we'll set it to bucket name.
>
> **[4:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=291)** Then you can define the targets which can be by parameter values, resource group, tags, or all instances.
>
> **[4:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=299)** For this example, I'll use tags.
>
> **[5:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=302)** I've already tagged my buckets, so I'll include the required tag key and tag value.
>
> **[5:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=307)** The tag key is environment and the tag value is production.
>
> **[5:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=312)** Scrolling down, we'll find the versioning state which we want set to enabled.
>
> **[5:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=318)** Here, you can provide an IAM role for the runbook.
>
> **[5:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=321)** The IAM role gives the service the necessary permission to perform actions on your behalf.
>
> **[5:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=327)** If you don't specify a role, it uses the context of your user profile.
>
> **[5:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=332)** For example, if your account has administrator permissions, then the automation runs with administrator permissions.
>
> **[5:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=339)** Here, we have rate control settings like concurrency and error threshold.
>
> **[5:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=344)** You can also configure a CloudWatch alarm, which when activated, will cause the execution to stop.
>
> **[5:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=350)** We'll leave these settings at the default and execute the runbook.
>
> **[5:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=355)** The executions have been successfully completed on the tagged buckets.
>
> **[6:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=360)** These buckets will now have versioning enabled on them.
>
> **[6:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=364)** As you can imagine, the automation capability can be useful to configure objects at scale.
>
> **[6:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=370)** Especially when used with AWS organizations, you can centrally apply automation actions from your management account.
>
> **[6:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/aws-systems-manager?u=76281980&t=377)** So that's about AWS Systems Manager automation.

#### Auto Scaling
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=0)** One of the goals of automation is to automatically scale your capacity based on demand.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=5)** That is, scale out or add more resources when demand is high and scale in or reduce resources when demand is low.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=14)** AWS Auto Scaling helps you do this.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=17)** It automatically scales resources based on your scaling strategy.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=21)** There are two Auto Scaling services available in the AWS Console; Amazon EC2 Auto Scaling and Application Auto Scaling.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=30)** Amazon EC2 Auto Scaling is available within the EC2 service and can be used to scale EC2 instances.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=37)** Application Auto Scaling is a separate service and can be used to scale resources such as Aurora replicas, DynamoDB tables, Amazon Elastic Container Service or ECS services, Spot Fleet requests, and more.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=53)** You will find the full list of supported resources in the AWS documentation.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=58)** Application Auto Scaling allows you to use scaling strategies or policies to determine when to scale resources.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=66)** You can configure target tracking scaling, step scaling, and schedule scaling.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=71)** Target tracking policy scales your application based on a target value for a CloudWatch metric, such as CPU utilization.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=79)** You select a metric and define its target value.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=83)** Auto Scaling will try to maintain the metric at the defined value.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=87)** This is similar to how a thermostat maintains a target temperature.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=92)** Let's say you have an application running on EC2 instances and want to maintain the average CPU utilization at 50%.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=99)** You can configure the target tracking policy to scale out when the CPU exceeds 50% to handle the increased load, and scale in when the CPU drops below 50% to reduce costs.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=111)** With step scaling, you can scale capacity based on the size of the CloudWatch alarm breach.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=117)** So the size of the scaling adjustment varies based on the magnitude of the alarm breach.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=122)** For example, you can scale out by five capacity units if CPU usage, reaches 50%, and you can scale out by ten capacity units if CPU usage reaches 70%.
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=134)** With step scaling, even after a scaling event, the adjustments can continue for additional alarm breaches.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=141)** So in the previous example, the policy will continue to monitor the metric after a scale out occurs when the CPU reaches 50%.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=149)** If the CPU reaches 70%, the policy will execute the configured action.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=155)** Unlike target scaling, step scaling is only available for limited resource types.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=161)** I recommend checking the AWS documentation for the list of supported resources, as it is likely to change over time.
>
> **[2:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=168)** Schedule scaling allows you to create schedule actions that increase or decrease capacity at specific times.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=175)** This option is useful to automatically scale your application based on predictable load changes.
>
> **[3:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=181)** Let's say your application starts receiving more traffic by Friday evening, and the traffic drops to normal levels by Sunday evening.
>
> **[3:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=189)** This is a good example to configure with schedule scaling.
>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=193)** For best results, you can combine schedule scaling with other scaling policies.
>
> **[3:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=199)** This allows you to get the benefits of proactive and reactive approaches.
>
> **[3:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=203)** So that's about Application Auto Scaling.
>
> **[3:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=206)** The other scaling service, that is Amazon EC2 Auto Scaling, also supports target tracking, step scaling, and schedule scaling.
>
> **[3:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=214)** Additionally, it also supports predictive scaling.
>
> **[3:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=218)** Predictive scaling analyzes historical load data to detect patterns in your traffic flows.
>
> **[3:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=224)** It uses this information to forecast capacity needs and proactively increases capacity to match the anticipated load.
>
> **[3:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=231)** Now, let's go to the AWS Management Console and see how to configure this.
>

>

> **[5:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=348)** I haven't registered my DynamoDB table as a target so scheduled scaling isn't available.
>
> **[5:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=353)** This is an important thing to remember. For step and schedule scaling, many resource types require you to register them as a scalable target.

>

>
> **[7:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=430)** Simple scaling is a simplified version of step scaling, which allows you to perform a single scaling adjustment.
>
> **[7:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=438)** AWS recommends using either target tracking or step scaling.

> **[7:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=461)** So that's about Auto Scaling.
>
> **[7:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/auto-scaling?u=76281980&t=463)** It is a simple yet powerful service that allows you to optimize resource utilization, improve performance, and make your solutions cost-efficient.

> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/other-automation-tools-in-aws?u=76281980&t=0)** So we've covered the important automation tools in AWS.
>
> **[0:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/other-automation-tools-in-aws?u=76281980&t=3)** Let's quickly talk about other tools to automate deployment and workflows.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/other-automation-tools-in-aws?u=76281980&t=9)** We talked about AWS Control Tower in an earlier video.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/other-automation-tools-in-aws?u=76281980&t=13)** It improves the security of your AWS environment by creating a landing zone with best practices.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/other-automation-tools-in-aws?u=76281980&t=19)** AWS Control Tower has a feature called Account Factory that automates the provisioning of pre-configured AWS accounts according to your security and compliance requirements.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/other-automation-tools-in-aws?u=76281980&t=29)** Amazon CloudWatch is a monitoring service that helps with creating automated workflows.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/other-automation-tools-in-aws?u=76281980&t=35)** Amazon CloudWatch monitors key metrics of your applications and resources, which you can use along with Amazon EventBridge to create an event-driven architecture.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/other-automation-tools-in-aws?u=76281980&t=46)** AWS Config is a tool used to improve the security and governance of resources by monitoring their configuration.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/other-automation-tools-in-aws?u=76281980&t=53)** It does this based on configured rules.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/other-automation-tools-in-aws?u=76281980&t=55)** Once configured, AWS Config automatically monitors your resources for compliance.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/other-automation-tools-in-aws?u=76281980&t=62)** You can also configure automatic remediation of non-compliant resources.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/other-automation-tools-in-aws?u=76281980&t=66)** Amazon SQS and SNS are tools commonly used to build automated workflows.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/other-automation-tools-in-aws?u=76281980&t=71)** Simple Queue Service is a message queuing service commonly used to decouple application components.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/other-automation-tools-in-aws?u=76281980&t=78)** Simple Notification Service is a message delivery service that allows automated delivery of messages or notifications from publishers to subscribers.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/other-automation-tools-in-aws?u=76281980&t=88)** Just like SQS, SNS can also be used to decouple components in automated workflows.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/other-automation-tools-in-aws?u=76281980&t=95)** So those are the important automation services to be aware of.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/other-automation-tools-in-aws?u=76281980&t=99)** As we've seen in this section of the course, embracing automation can make your solutions robust, scalable, and efficient.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/other-automation-tools-in-aws?u=76281980&t=106)** Automation can help you orchestrate complex workflows and enforce best practices through code-driven deployments.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/other-automation-tools-in-aws?u=76281980&t=114)** Embracing automation will liberate you from manual, error-prone and mundane operational tasks, allowing you to focus on innovation and strategic initiatives.

>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/designing-a-strategy-for-improving-performance?u=76281980&t=54)** It allows you to try without impacting production workloads.

> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/designing-a-strategy-for-improving-performance?u=76281980&t=58)** Use scalable services.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/designing-a-strategy-for-improving-performance?u=76281980&t=60)** Fully-managed services are designed to handle massive workloads and fluctuations in demand while maintaining performance.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/designing-a-strategy-for-improving-performance?u=76281980&t=67)** For example, managed services like Amazon S3, RDS, DynamoDB, and others are designed to handle large scale deployments.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/designing-a-strategy-for-improving-performance?u=76281980&t=76)** Consider serverless architectures.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/designing-a-strategy-for-improving-performance?u=76281980&t=79)** With serverless architectures, you do not need to maintain servers for compute activities like running code.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/designing-a-strategy-for-improving-performance?u=76281980&t=85)** This approach eliminates the operational burden of managing servers and accelerates the speed of deployment, improving the performance of your solutions.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/designing-a-strategy-for-improving-performance?u=76281980&t=94)** Deploy globally.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/designing-a-strategy-for-improving-performance?u=76281980&t=96)** Deploying your solutions in multiple locations reduces latency and provides a better customer experience.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/designing-a-strategy-for-improving-performance?u=76281980&t=103)** Cost is a common concern when deploying globally.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/designing-a-strategy-for-improving-performance?u=76281980&t=106)** The cost impact of a global deployment can be offset or mitigated by deploying only the required resources.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/designing-a-strategy-for-improving-performance?u=76281980&t=113)** Services like Auto Scaling can be used to maintain the required capacity to handle the workloads and reduce unnecessary costs.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/designing-a-strategy-for-improving-performance?u=76281980&t=121)** Maintain an inventory of your resources.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/designing-a-strategy-for-improving-performance?u=76281980&t=124)** Having an updated inventory allows architects to clearly understand the resources deployed in their environment.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/designing-a-strategy-for-improving-performance?u=76281980&t=131)** This visibility allows for better resource management and optimization efforts to improve performance.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/designing-a-strategy-for-improving-performance?u=76281980&t=137)** Select the best service for your workload.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/designing-a-strategy-for-improving-performance?u=76281980&t=141)** AWS has many services with overlapping functionalities, so choosing the right service for your workload is essential.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/designing-a-strategy-for-improving-performance?u=76281980&t=148)** Important domains like compute, storage, databases, and compliance have multiple services for different use cases and may have overlapping functionalities.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/designing-a-strategy-for-improving-performance?u=76281980&t=159)** For example, you can use an EC2 instance to run code or use Lambda, which is a serverless service.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/designing-a-strategy-for-improving-performance?u=76281980&t=166)** It is important to consider the requirements of your workload like traffic patterns, throughput, and latency requirements.

> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/designing-a-strategy-for-improving-performance?u=76281980&t=190)** And lastly, test performance.

#### Monitoring with CloudWatch
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=0)** Ensuring optimal performance is key to meeting user expectations and business objectives, and ensuring optimal performance requires continuous monitoring.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=9)** Amazon CloudWatch allows you to monitor your AWS resources and applications in real time.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=15)** You can use CloudWatch to collect and track metrics, which are performance indicators of your resources.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=21)** Each AWS service has predefined metrics that CloudWatch monitors, but you can also publish your own custom metrics.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=28)** You can also use CloudWatch to collect and monitor log files from your applications and to set alarms.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=35)** Each metric has either standard or high resolution.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=38)** Standard resolution has a one-minute granularity, while high resolution has a one-second granularity.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=45)** By default, metrics produced by AWS services have standard resolution.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=49)** High resolution metrics can give you immediate insights into your applications performance.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=54)** A CloudWatch alarm tracks a single metric over a specified period.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=59)** For example, you can have an alarm track the CPU utilization metric.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=63)** You can use an alarm to initiate actions on your behalf automatically.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=68)** For example, if the average CPU usage is over 70% for five minutes, you can have Auto Scaling add more EC2 instances to maintain desired performance levels.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=79)** CloudWatch also allows you to create dashboards to monitor resources in a single view.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=84)** The resources may be spread across different AWS regions and different AWS accounts.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=89)** CloudWatch has an agent that you can use to collect internal system level metrics from EC2 instances that are not natively collected by the EC2 service, for example, disk and memory related metrics.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=102)** You can also use the agent to collect system level metrics from your on-premises servers, and retrieve custom metrics from your applications.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=110)** CloudWatch has an Internet monitor feature that allows you to monitor Internet availability and performance issues between your AWS-hosted applications and their end users.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=121)** It can help you quickly identify Internet-related issues that may be degrading your applications performance.
>
> **[2:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=127)** Another feature called Network Monitor allows you to view the performance of the network connecting your AWS-hosted applications to your on-premises destinations.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=137)** You can use it to identify issues such as packet loss and latency that might impact your applications performance.
>
> **[2:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=143)** Now, let's go to the AWS Management Console and see things in action.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=149)** From the Management Console, you will find CloudWatch under the "Management and Governance" section.
>
> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=156)** Once you're here, you will see any configured alarms or your default dashboard.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=162)** Under the dashboard section, you will find your custom dashboards and out-of-the-box dashboards provided by AWS.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=170)** The automatic dashboards you see here will depend on the services used in your account.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=176)** Click on your dashboard to view the metrics.
>
> **[2:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=179)** You can change the period, timezone, and other settings from here.
>
> **[3:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=184)** Alarms can be configured from here.
>
> **[3:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=188)** You have the default billing alarm that you can use to monitor your AWS bill and alert you when charges exceed the defined threshold.
>
> **[3:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=196)** Additional alarms can be created from here.
>
> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=200)** To create an alarm, you select a metric.
>
> **[3:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=202)** This is the variable or performance indicator you want to track.
>
> **[3:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=207)** The options you see here are based on services used in your account.
>
> **[3:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=211)** Select the desired service, the metric type, and then the metric to track.
>
> **[3:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=217)** Here, I'm selecting the CPU utilization metric for an EC2 instance.
>
> **[3:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=223)** Then you can define how you want to track the metric, such as the statistic, monitoring period, and the threshold type.
>
> **[3:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=232)** This configuration will trigger the alarm when the CPU usage for the instance goes above 70%.
>
> **[3:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=239)** In the next step, you can define actions to take when the alarm triggers.
>
> **[4:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=245)** You can trigger a notification or perform an Auto Scaling action.
>
> **[4:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/monitoring-with-cloudwatch?u=76281980&t=249)** For now, I'll remove these and provide a name for the alarm in the next step.

>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/gathering-performance-insights?u=76281980&t=48)** A log group is a group of log streams that share the same settings like retention, monitoring, and access control.

#### Using a content delivery network
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/using-a-content-delivery-network?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/using-a-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=0)** Content delivery networks are commonly used to improve application performance.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/using-a-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=5)** A content delivery network is a group of servers distributed around the world to cache content close to end users.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/using-a-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=12)** Amazon CloudFront is a content delivery service that speeds up the distribution of static and dynamic web content to your users.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/using-a-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=20)** It delivers your content through a network of data centers called edge locations.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/using-a-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=26)** Imagine this.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/using-a-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=27)** You have a web server in London.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/using-a-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=30)** When users around the world try to access your website or application, their requests have to travel to London and back.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/using-a-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=38)** This increases latency. With CloudFront, when a user requests content, the request is routed to the edge location that provides the lowest latency.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/using-a-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=48)** CloudFront delivers the content immediately if it is already in the edge location with the lowest latency.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/using-a-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=55)** If content is not in the edge location, CloudFront retrieves it from the origin and delivers it to the user.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/using-a-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=62)** It also caches the content for the next time someone requests it.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/using-a-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=67)** The origin can be an HTTP server, like a web server or even an S3 bucket.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/using-a-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=73)** CloudFront routes each user request through the AWS backbone network, not the public Internet.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/using-a-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=80)** Using the AWS backbone reduces the number of networks the users request must pass through, improving performance.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/using-a-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=88)** It also improves availability because copies of your files are held or cached in multiple edge locations worldwide.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/using-a-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=95)** Configuring CloudFront is straightforward.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/using-a-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=98)** You create a CloudFront distribution to tell CloudFront which origin servers to get your files from when users request them.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/using-a-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=105)** You then upload files to your origin servers.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/using-a-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=108)** This typically includes web pages, images, and media files, but it can be anything that can be delivered over HTTP.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/using-a-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=116)** When you create a distribution, CloudFront assigns it a domain name.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/using-a-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=120)** You can also configure CloudFront to use your own domain name.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/using-a-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=124)** To deliver content through CloudFront, you must access it using the CloudFront distribution URL or the custom domain name if you've configured one.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/using-a-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=133)** CloudFront is commonly used for website acceleration.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/using-a-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=137)** You can speed up delivery of static content such as images, media files, and software downloads, and dynamic content such as HTML or PHP pages.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/using-a-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=146)** CloudFront is also used for global content distribution.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/using-a-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=150)** CloudFront distributes content across multiple regions without requiring a server in each region.
>
> **[2:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/using-a-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=157)** You can also use CloudFront for secure content delivery.
>
> **[2:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/using-a-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=160)** CloudFront supports HTTPS, so you have secure end-to-end connections.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/using-a-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=166)** You can also use CloudFront for video streaming.
>
> **[2:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/using-a-content-delivery-network?u=76281980&t=169)** CloudFront supports both pre-recorded video files and live events.

#### Caching
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/caching?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/caching?u=76281980&t=0)** Caching is a technique used to improve the performance of applications.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/caching?u=76281980&t=5)** It is often the most significant factor in creating an application that performs well at scale.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/caching?u=76281980&t=10)** Popular applications like e-commerce, gaming, and social media rely on caching to deliver high performance.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/caching?u=76281980&t=18)** It involves storing copies of data in a temporary storage location known as a cache, so users can access them quickly.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/caching?u=76281980&t=26)** When data is stored on storage disks, it is slower to retrieve.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/caching?u=76281980&t=30)** With caching, data is stored in fast access hardware such as random-access memory or RAM.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/caching?u=76281980&t=37)** Doing so lets you offload read request from your database to the cache, improving performance.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/caching?u=76281980&t=44)** In this video, we'll cover the different caching services available with AWS.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/caching?u=76281980&t=49)** The most well-known caching service is Amazon ElastiCache.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/caching?u=76281980&t=54)** It is a fully managed in-memory cache for your web applications.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/caching?u=76281980&t=58)** It improves performance by storing critical pieces of data in memory for fast access.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/caching?u=76281980&t=64)** Doing so improves latency and throughput, especially for read-heavy applications.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/caching?u=76281980&t=71)** As a managed service, AWS takes care of the details like provisioning the resources, installing the software, detecting failure, and patching.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/caching?u=76281980&t=80)** ElastiCache supports Redis and Memcached; the two popular caching engines. A simple application deployment without caching consists of a front end web and application tier, and a backend database tier.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/caching?u=76281980&t=94)** When you deploy ElastiCache, it is a separate tier alongside your database.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/caching?u=76281980&t=100)** As requests come in to the web tier, the instances communicate with ElastiCache and the database tier.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/caching?u=76281980&t=106)** ElastiCache helps to improve response time by caching frequently accessed data.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/caching?u=76281980&t=112)** While ElastiCache aims to improve web application performance, Amazon File Cache provides a managed high-speed cache for processing file data.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/caching?u=76281980&t=121)** You can use it to cache data stored in on-premises file systems, AWS file systems, and Amazon S3 buckets.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/caching?u=76281980&t=130)** It is suitable for file-based applications that quickly process large volumes of data, such as data analysis and simulation workloads.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/caching?u=76281980&t=139)** If you're using Amazon DynamoDB as your database solution, you can configure DynamoDB accelerator or DAX as the in-memory cache.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/caching?u=76281980&t=148)** DAX is ideal for applications that require the fastest possible response time for reads, for example, gaming and trading applications.
>
> **[2:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/caching?u=76281980&t=158)** DAX reduces the response time from milliseconds to microseconds.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/caching?u=76281980&t=163)** DAX is also ideal for applications that read a small number of items more frequently than others, like news websites.
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/caching?u=76281980&t=171)** As a managed service, AWS manages the complexities like data population and resource management.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/caching?u=76281980&t=178)** And lastly, Amazon CloudFront, a content delivery network, also has caching capabilities.
>
> **[3:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/caching?u=76281980&t=186)** It caches copies of your content in multiple locations worldwide, reducing response time and load on your servers and improving the end user experience by delivering content from the location closest to the user.
>
> **[3:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/caching?u=76281980&t=199)** So those are the main caching solutions available in AWS.
>
> **[3:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/caching?u=76281980&t=203)** The key to successful caching is understanding your applications requirements, access patterns, and data characteristics.
>
> **[3:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/caching?u=76281980&t=211)** Including caching solutions in your architecture will enhance application performance, scalability, and end user experience.

#### High-performance storage
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/high-performance-storage?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/high-performance-storage?u=76281980&t=0)** Now, let's talk about high-performance storage options available with AWS.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/high-performance-storage?u=76281980&t=4)** Amazon Elastic Block Store or EBS, provides block level storage volumes for use with EC2 instances.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/high-performance-storage?u=76281980&t=12)** You mount these volumes to your instances and use them like you would use a physical hard drive.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/high-performance-storage?u=76281980&t=18)** EBS volumes are available in different types.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/high-performance-storage?u=76281980&t=20)** Solid-state drive or SSD volumes, hard disk drive or HDD volumes, and magnetic volumes.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/high-performance-storage?u=76281980&t=28)** SSD volumes generally provide better performance than HDD volumes.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/high-performance-storage?u=76281980&t=33)** SSD volumes are available as general purpose and provisioned IOPS volumes.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/high-performance-storage?u=76281980&t=37)** Provisioned IOPS volumes provide the highest performance for SSD volumes.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/high-performance-storage?u=76281980&t=42)** They are designed for critical IOPS intensive and throughput intensive workloads that require low latency.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/high-performance-storage?u=76281980&t=49)** Provisioned IOPS volumes provide sub millisecond latency, storage capacity up to 64 TB bytes, IOPS up to 256,000, and volume throughput up to 4,000 MiB/s.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/high-performance-storage?u=76281980&t=64)** So provision IOPS volumes can be a good fit for high-performance databases, big data, high-performance computing and e-commerce systems.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/high-performance-storage?u=76281980&t=73)** Amazon Elastic File System, or EFS, is another high-performance storage.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/high-performance-storage?u=76281980&t=79)** It is a serverless elastic file storage designed for use with Linux-based applications.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/high-performance-storage?u=76281980&t=85)** You can use it to provide file storage for EC2 instances and on-premises servers.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/high-performance-storage?u=76281980&t=90)** When configuring EFS, you can create a regional or one-zone file system.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/high-performance-storage?u=76281980&t=95)** Regional file systems provide better performance because they can tolerate the failure of one or more availability zones in an AWS region.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/high-performance-storage?u=76281980&t=104)** When configuring EFS, you can also specify the throughput mode, which can be elastic, provisioned, or bursting.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/high-performance-storage?u=76281980&t=112)** Elastic throughput mode is best when you have spiky or unpredictable workloads, and you cannot forecast performance requirements.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/high-performance-storage?u=76281980&t=120)** Provisioned throughput mode allows you to specify the throughput level, so it is a good choice if you know your workloads performance requirements.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/high-performance-storage?u=76281980&t=128)** Bursting throughput is best when you want throughput that scales with the amount of storage in your file system.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/high-performance-storage?u=76281980&t=135)** So the best performing throughput mode depends on your workload requirements.
>
> **[2:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/high-performance-storage?u=76281980&t=140)** Amazon FS is a similar service.
>
> **[2:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/high-performance-storage?u=76281980&t=143)** It allows you to create high-performance file systems.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/high-performance-storage?u=76281980&t=146)** Amazon FSX for Lustre allows you to create a fully managed Lustre file system.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/high-performance-storage?u=76281980&t=151)** Lustre is an open source file system for high-performance workloads like machine learning, high-performance computing, and financial modeling.
>
> **[2:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/high-performance-storage?u=76281980&t=160)** Setting up a Lustre file system is a complex operation requiring extensive planning and configuration.
>
> **[2:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/high-performance-storage?u=76281980&t=167)** Amazon FSX for Lustre makes it easy to set up a Lustre file system in minutes.
>
> **[2:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/high-performance-storage?u=76281980&t=173)** Amazon S3 is an object storage service in AWS.
>
> **[2:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/high-performance-storage?u=76281980&t=177)** S3 offers a range of storage classes designed for different use cases based on data access, resiliency, and cost requirements.
>
> **[3:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/high-performance-storage?u=76281980&t=186)** S3 Express One Zone is a high-performance storage class that delivers single digit millisecond data access.
>
> **[3:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/high-performance-storage?u=76281980&t=192)** It is suitable for latency sensitive applications such as media content creation, machine learning, and interactive analytics. So those are the high-performance storage options available with AWS.
>
> **[3:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/high-performance-storage?u=76281980&t=204)** As we've just seen, there are several options to meet the demands of modern applications and workloads.
>
> **[3:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/high-performance-storage?u=76281980&t=210)** Understanding your applications requirements is key to effectively leveraging these storage solutions.
>
> **[3:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/high-performance-storage?u=76281980&t=216)** You can build high-performing, scalable, and efficient solutions by strategically selecting these services.
