#### Hybrid Storage
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=0)** Using hybrid storage can provide performance enhancement for organizations that want to leverage the benefits of both on-premises and cloud environments.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=9)** It can also be a good option for organizations that cannot move their workloads to the cloud, but want to use cloud technologies.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=17)** Hybrid cloud storage connects your on-premises applications and systems to cloud storage.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=23)** In addition to performance benefits, hybrid cloud storage reduces operational burden as the services are fully managed.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=30)** Let's talk about the services you can use for hybrid cloud storage.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=34)** AWS Storage Gateway is the most popular hybrid cloud storage service.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=39)** It provides cloud-based storage to your on-premises applications.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=43)** Because it uses standard storage protocols such as iSCSI, SMB, and NFS, you do not need to rewrite your existing applications to make them work with storage gateway.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=54)** You can use it to provide on-premises applications with low latency access to data stored in AWS, reduce on-premises storage with cloud backed file shares, and move backup and archives to the cloud.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=68)** Storage Gateway provides three interface options; file, volume, and tape.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=76)** We spoke about these in an earlier video of the course.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=79)** The File Gateway option allows storing and retrieving objects in Amazon S3 or Amazon FSX for Windows File Server.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=88)** The Volume Gateway option provides block storage volumes to your on-premises applications.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=93)** Data on the volumes is stored in Amazon S3.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=96)** The Tape Gateway option provides your backup application with a virtual tape library.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=102)** Virtual tapes are stored in Amazon S3.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=105)** Tape Gateway can free administrators from the operational complexities of managing physical tapes.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=112)** Once the data is in S3, you can archive it to S3 Glacier, a low cost storage class.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=120)** The Storage Gateway appliance is available as a virtual and hardware appliance.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=125)** Another related service is AWS DataSync.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=129)** It is an online data transfer service that moves data between on-premises storage systems and AWS, between AWS storage services and between other cloud storage systems in AWS.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=142)** For transferring from on-premise systems, DataSync supports Network File System or NFS, Server Message Block or SMB, Hadoop Distributed File Systems, or HDFS, and other object storage.
>
> **[2:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=158)** For transferring between AWS services, DataSync supports Amazon S3, Amazon Elastic File System, and Amazon FSX.
>
> **[2:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=167)** For transferring from other cloud storage systems, DataSync supports popular services like Google Cloud storage, Azure Blob storage, Azure Files, Oracle Cloud Infrastructure Object Storage, and more.
>
> **[3:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=181)** You can use DataSync to discover data.
>
> **[3:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=183)** Doing so gives you visibility into your on-premises storage performance and utilization.
>
> **[3:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=189)** After discovery, DataSync provides recommendations for migrating your data to AWS storage.
>
> **[3:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=195)** You can also use DataSync to migrate data and archive cold data that is moved from on-premises cold storage directly to cold storage in AWS, allowing you to free up on-premises storage capacity and shut down the use of legacy systems.
>
> **[3:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=211)** Another service called AWS Transfer Family allows you to transfer files over File Transfer Protocol or FTP, File Transfer Protocol Secure or FTPS, Secure Shell File Transfer Protocol, or SFTP, and Applicability Statement 2 or AS2.
>
> **[3:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=230)** You can transfer the files into and out of Amazon S3 or Amazon Elastic File System.
>
> **[3:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=236)** These protocols are commonly used for business-to-business file transfers, like transferring files to customers, third-party suppliers, and stakeholders.
>
> **[4:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=246)** Using Transfer Family frees your administrators from creating and managing a file transfer service, which can be an operationally challenging task.
>
> **[4:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=254)** Lastly, let's talk about AWS Snowball.
>
> **[4:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=258)** AWS Snowball provides physical devices that you can use to migrate data to AWS.
>
> **[4:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=264)** It is useful when Internet bandwidth isn't available for online transfer services such as AWS DataSync.
>
> **[4:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=270)** You begin by setting up a job in the AWS Snowball Console, and then AWS ships you a Snowball device known as Snowball Edge.
>
> **[4:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=279)** After receiving the device, you transfer data to it and ship it back to AWS.
>
> **[4:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=284)** AWS then ingests the data to Amazon S3 in your account.
>
> **[4:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=289)** In addition to storage, Snowball Edge devices also have onboard computing capabilities.
>
> **[4:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=295)** So you can use it to run compute services like EC2 instances in rugged, disconnected, and remote locations.
>
> **[5:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=303)** Snowball Edge doesn't require Internet connectivity, so data transfer and compute activities can occur in isolated environments.
>
> **[5:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=311)** So those are the hybrid storage options available with AWS.
>
> **[5:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=315)** Each serves a unique purpose in the hybrid storage ecosystem.
>
> **[5:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/hybrid-storage?u=76281980&t=319)** When selecting a hybrid storage option, consider specific requirements such as data volume, network bandwidth, transfer frequency, and operational overhead.

#### Managed databases
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/managed-databases?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/managed-databases?u=76281980&t=0)** When you want to run a database on AWS, you have two design choices.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/managed-databases?u=76281980&t=5)** You can install the database on an EC2 instance and self-manage it or use a managed database.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/managed-databases?u=76281980&t=12)** A managed database is where AWS manages it and you simply host your data on it.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/managed-databases?u=76281980&t=17)** Using a managed database has several advantages.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/managed-databases?u=76281980&t=21)** It leads to better performance.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/managed-databases?u=76281980&t=23)** Managed databases have configuration options for specific needs like I/O intensive workloads, and they are designed to handle large volumes of data. Managed databases reduce operational burden. AWS handles operational tasks like provisioning, scaling, patching, backups, and failover.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/managed-databases?u=76281980&t=43)** Managed databases are automatically configured for high availability, with options to deploy in multiple locations to further improve availability, performance, and disaster recovery.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/managed-databases?u=76281980&t=54)** Managed databases support automated backups, reducing the administrative burden of managing them. And like most cloud services, managed databases have pay-as-you-go pricing so you only pay for what you use.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/managed-databases?u=76281980&t=67)** There are several managed database offerings in AWS.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/managed-databases?u=76281980&t=71)** Here are the important ones.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/managed-databases?u=76281980&t=73)** If you're looking for relational databases, you have Amazon RDS or Relational Database Service and Amazon Aurora.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/managed-databases?u=76281980&t=81)** If you're looking for a data warehouse solution, you have Amazon Redshift.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/managed-databases?u=76281980&t=86)** For non-relational or NoSQL workloads, you can use Amazon DynamoDB.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/managed-databases?u=76281980&t=91)** If you're looking for an in-memory caching service to improve the performance of your applications, consider Amazon ElastiCache.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/managed-databases?u=76281980&t=99)** If you need a MongoDB-compliant document database service, you have Amazon DocumentDB. To work with graph data on AWS, you can use Amazon Neptune.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/managed-databases?u=76281980&t=110)** Each managed database is optimized for performance.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/managed-databases?u=76281980&t=114)** Vendor lock-in is a common consideration when using managed databases.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/managed-databases?u=76281980&t=118)** However, their performance and operational benefits outweigh this consideration.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/managed-databases?u=76281980&t=123)** Including these in your solution architecture can streamline operational tasks and free up your developers to build better solutions rather than manage infrastructure.

### 5. Optimize for Cost

> [[#Table of Contents|↑ Back to Table of Contents]]

#### Strategies for optimizing costs
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=0)** When hosting your systems and applications in the cloud, it is important to understand how the billing model works and how you can optimize costs.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=8)** Controlling costs is as critical as ensuring performance and security.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=13)** It ensures that you're not just using the technology efficiently, but also maximizing the value of your spending.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=20)** Let's discuss strategies to minimize your costs while maximizing performance.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=25)** Understand pricing models.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=28)** Most AWS services have pay-as-you-go pricing.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=31)** This means you only pay for what you use.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=34)** But within this pricing model, services have configurations that can optimize your overall costs.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=40)** For example, with EC2 instances, you can opt for on-demand instances or use savings plans which give you a billing discount.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=49)** Similarly, with Amazon S3, your pricing depends on the amount of data you store and the storage class you choose.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=57)** Understanding the pricing model will enable you to choose the most cost-effective option for your specific use case.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=65)** Rightsize your resources.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=67)** Most AWS services and resources have different configurations for different performance use cases.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=73)** Using the most appropriate configuration that meets your performance requirements is essential.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=79)** Under sizing resources can lead to performance issues, and over sizing could lead to unnecessary costs.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=86)** In this sense, auditing regularly for underutilized and unused resources is important.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=92)** Use Auto Scaling.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=94)** Many AWS services, such as compute and databases, have Auto Scaling options.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=99)** This means scaling up when demand is high and scaling down when demand is low.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=104)** Utilizing Auto Scaling is an efficient way to match supply with demand and optimize costs.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=110)** Manage data transfer costs. While resource utilization costs are accounted for, it is easy to overlook data transfer costs.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=119)** These can quickly add up and significantly impact your budget.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=124)** To optimize data transfer costs, you can avoid routing traffic over the Internet when connecting to AWS services from within AWS.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=133)** You can do this using VPC endpoints for supported services.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=137)** Doing so ensures traffic does not leave the Amazon network.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=141)** You will find more information about this in the AWS documentation.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=145)** To optimize data transfer costs between your on-premises environment and AWS, consider using Direct Connect.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=152)** It is a dedicated connection exclusively for your use and does not incur standard Internet data transfer charges.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=159)** Implement governance.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=161)** Governance is critical to controlling cloud expenditures.
>
> **[2:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=165)** Develop policies for resource provisioning and use of cost effective regions and services.
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=171)** Also, implement a tagging policy to categorize resources by owner, cost center, environment, project, and other criteria.
>
> **[3:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=180)** Effective tagging can help with tracking costs and implementing chargebacks.
>
> **[3:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=186)** Use Identity and Access Management, or IAM to ensure users and applications have access only to the required resources.
>
> **[3:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=194)** Limiting access can prevent unintended or unauthorized resource provisioning, controlling costs.
>
> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=200)** Measure spending.
>
> **[3:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=202)** To optimize costs, you need visibility into where and how you're incurring them.
>
> **[3:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=207)** AWS has tools that help you understand where you're spending the most and provide recommendations to reduce unnecessary spending.
>
> **[3:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=215)** This includes tools like Cost Explorer and cost allocation tags.
>
> **[3:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=219)** We'll talk about these in a later video.
>
> **[3:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=222)** Conduct regular audits of your environments to ensure compliance with governance policies, and identify areas to reduce unnecessary spending.
>
> **[3:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/strategies-for-optimizing-costs?u=76281980&t=231)** With these strategies in mind, let's dive into the details of reducing compute and storage costs.

#### Reducing compute costs
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=0)** Compute is usually the most significant spend in the cloud.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=4)** AWS has different compute services, including Amazon EC2, AWS Lambda, Amazon Elastic Container Service or ECS, Elastic Beanstalk, and more.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=16)** The first step in cost optimization is understanding these services and their use cases.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=21)** Use the AWS documentation to understand which service may be best to handle your workload.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=27)** Consider the following strategies to reduce your compute costs.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=31)** Right-size EC2 instances.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=35)** AWS has many EC2 instance families like general purpose, compute optimized, memory optimized, storage optimized, and more.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=44)** Each instance family has many instance types or sizes.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=48)** Each instance type and family is optimized for specific use cases.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=52)** For example, the T3 instance type, part of the general purpose family, is ideal for web servers, small databases, and development environments.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=62)** Meanwhile, the C5 instance type, part of the compute optimized family, is ideal for use cases such as batch processing, scientific modeling, and other high-performance computing.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=74)** Use the AWS documentation to understand which instance type may be appropriate for your use case.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=80)** Once deployed, use Amazon CloudWatch to monitor usage of your resource.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=85)** If usage is consistently less, you may be able to downsize without impacting performance, reducing costs.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=92)** Utilize Spot instances.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=95)** Spot instances are an EC2 purchasing option that allow you to request unused EC2 capacity for lower than on-demand rates.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=103)** In some cases, you can save up to 90% on on-demand prices.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=108)** The caveat is that AWS may interrupt or terminate these instances with a two-minute warning.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=114)** Architecting your applications to handle interruptions will allow you to take advantage of Spot instances.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=121)** A common strategy is to use a combination of on-demand and spot instances to handle workloads.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=128)** If the spot instances get interrupted, on-demand instances in the fleet can continue to process the workload.
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=134)** Leverage reserved instances and savings plans.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=137)** Reserved instances and savings plans offer significant discounts when you commit to a one-year or three-year term.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=144)** These options are excellent for long-term projects with predictable usage.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=149)** Implement Auto Scaling.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=152)** Auto Scaling is critical to managing costs and resource efficiency.
>
> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=156)** Once configured, Auto Scaling will automatically add and remove instances as required to handle the workload.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=164)** This means you're not under or overprovisioning, leading to cost savings.
>
> **[2:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=169)** Adopt serverless.
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=171)** Using serverless technologies like AWS Lambda can speed up deployment and significantly reduce costs because you're only paying when your code runs.
>
> **[3:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=180)** Serverless deployment also helps create event-driven architectures where you can run code in response to events.
>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=187)** Also, serverless deployments scale automatically.
>
> **[3:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=191)** Consolidate workloads.
>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=193)** Consolidating workloads involves combining multiple workloads or applications into fewer instances to maximize resource utilization.
>
> **[3:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=203)** Imagine a company with three low utilized web applications running on separate T3 medium instances.
>
> **[3:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=210)** It may be possible to consolidate these onto a single T3 large instance.
>
> **[3:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=216)** Begin by identifying underutilized instances and evaluate workloads for compatibility to ensure they can be consolidated.
>
> **[3:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=224)** After consolidation, continuously monitor performance to ensure that consolidation delivers the expected outcomes.
>
> **[3:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=231)** Use tools to understand usage and receive recommendations.
>
> **[3:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=236)** AWS has tools such as Compute Optimizer and Trusted Advisor that analyze your usage and provide recommendations to improve performance and reduce costs.
>
> **[4:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=246)** AWS Compute Optimizer identifies under provisioned, over provisioned, and optimized EC2 instances, Auto Scaling groups, Lambda functions, and Amazon Elastic Container Service or ECS services on Fargate.
>
> **[4:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=262)** AWS Trusted Advisor recommendations to reduce costs include; reserved instance optimization, idle load balancers, underutilized EC2 instances, overprovisioned memory size for Lambda functions, Unassociated Elastic IP addresses, and more.
>
> **[4:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=279)** Those are some strategies you can leverage to reduce compute costs.
>
> **[4:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-compute-costs?u=76281980&t=283)** It requires tools, a deep understanding of workloads, and stakeholder involvement.

#### Reducing storage costs
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-storage-costs?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-storage-costs?u=76281980&t=0)** After compute, storage is probably the second most significant spend in the cloud.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-storage-costs?u=76281980&t=5)** Let's look at strategies to reduce your storage costs.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-storage-costs?u=76281980&t=8)** Understand your storage needs.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-storage-costs?u=76281980&t=12)** AWS has storage services for different use cases like Amazon S3, Amazon Elastic File System or EFS, Amazon FSX, and Amazon Elastic Block Store or EBS.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-storage-costs?u=76281980&t=24)** Start by reviewing your current and future storage needs then review the different storage options as each has its pricing model and performance characteristics.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-storage-costs?u=76281980&t=34)** Choosing the appropriate storage service for your use case is an essential first step in controlling costs.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-storage-costs?u=76281980&t=40)** Leverage S3 lifecycle policies. When using Amazon S3 for object storage, lifecycle policies can help to move data to cheaper storage classes and delete expired data.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-storage-costs?u=76281980&t=53)** You can significantly reduce storage costs by moving less frequently accessed data to low cost storage classes and deleting data that is no longer needed.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-storage-costs?u=76281980&t=62)** You can use lifecycle policies to automate this process.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-storage-costs?u=76281980&t=66)** Use S3 intelligent-tiering. Storage classes such as standard and infrequent access are useful when you know your data access patterns.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-storage-costs?u=76281980&t=76)** For data with unpredictable or unknown access patterns, S3 intelligent-tiering is useful.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-storage-costs?u=76281980&t=82)** It moves data to the most cost-effective tier based on access frequency, reducing costs and operational overhead. Archive data.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-storage-costs?u=76281980&t=90)** Long-term data retention for data preservation and compliance purposes can add to storage costs.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-storage-costs?u=76281980&t=97)** Use the Amazon S3 Glacier storage class for cold data or data you want to retain for long periods.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-storage-costs?u=76281980&t=104)** Using S3 Glacier to archive your data can significantly reduce your storage costs.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-storage-costs?u=76281980&t=110)** You can use lifecycle policies to transition data to S3 Glacier.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-storage-costs?u=76281980&t=115)** Leverage EFS lifecycle policies.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-storage-costs?u=76281980&t=118)** Amazon Elastic File System, or EFS, has the infrequent access and archive storage classes for data that doesn't need to be frequently accessed.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-storage-costs?u=76281980&t=128)** You can use lifecycle policies to transition data to these storage classes and reduce your storage costs.
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-storage-costs?u=76281980&t=134)** Review EBS volumes. With services like Amazon S3 and Amazon EFS, you are charged for the amount of data stored.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-storage-costs?u=76281980&t=144)** But with Amazon EBS, you are charged for the size of the volume provisioned.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-storage-costs?u=76281980&t=149)** Let's say you create a provisioned IOPS EBS volume of 1 TB size with 10,000 IOPS or input outputs per second.
>
> **[2:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-storage-costs?u=76281980&t=158)** The original plan was to use this volume for a critical web application.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-storage-costs?u=76281980&t=163)** Later upon review, you find that peak IOPS usage rarely exceeds 3000 IOPS, and the storage used is about 200 GB.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-storage-costs?u=76281980&t=172)** However, you are still charged for the provision configuration, 1 TB storage and 10,000 IOPS.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-storage-costs?u=76281980&t=178)** Regular audits and continuous monitoring can help identify overprovision volumes.
>
> **[3:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-storage-costs?u=76281980&t=184)** Consider resizing them.
>
> **[3:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-storage-costs?u=76281980&t=186)** Another common reason for unnecessary costs with EBS is orphaned volumes.
>
> **[3:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-storage-costs?u=76281980&t=192)** These are volumes no longer attached to an EC2 instance.
>
> **[3:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-storage-costs?u=76281980&t=196)** Consider deleting them.
>
> **[3:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-storage-costs?u=76281980&t=198)** So those are the important strategies you can implement to reduce storage costs.
>
> **[3:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/reducing-storage-costs?u=76281980&t=202)** Lastly, remember that these tasks are not a one-time exercise, but rather ongoing and continuous.

> **Env Vars:** ebs (5), iops (5), efs (4), aws (1), fsx (1)

#### Tools to track cost and usage
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=0)** Now, let's talk about tools to track cost and usage.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=4)** Let's start with the AWS Pricing Calculator.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=7)** It is an online tool that allows you to estimate the cost of your solution.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=12)** You can add the services you're likely to use with your solution, and it will show you the estimated costs per service and the totals.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=20)** AWS Cost Explorer is a tool that allows you to view and analyze your costs and usage.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=26)** It gives you a breakdown of costs incurred from every AWS service you use.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=31)** It allows you to view data for up to the last 13 months and forecast how much you're likely to spend for the next 12 months.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=38)** You can use filters to drill down to the details and download the data as a CSV file.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=44)** AWS Budgets allows you to set a monthly cost budget with a fixed or variable target amount.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=51)** AWS Budgets can alert you for actual and forecasted spending.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=55)** Cost allocation tags allow you to categorize and track your AWS costs.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=59)** There are two types of cost allocation tags; AWS-generated and user-defined.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=65)** Once activated, these tags appear in Cost Explorer and cost and usage reports.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=71)** If you're using AWS Organizations, AWS automatically consolidates charges for the member accounts into the management account.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=80)** When viewing your bills, you can view charges by member accounts and then break them down further to view charges per service.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=87)** Now, let's go to the AWS Management Console and see these tools.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=92)** Here, I'm logged in as the root user of this account.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=95)** Once you're here, click your name on the top right corner and then navigate to Billing and Cost Management.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=102)** From here, click "Pricing calculator" on the left navigation pane.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=107)** Doing so will open the tool in a new browser tab.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=111)** You can also access this tool without logging into your AWS account.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=116)** You can create an estimate by adding the required services.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=120)** Find the required service and then click "Configure."
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=125)** Now, add the details to generate your estimated usage.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=129)** For example, with the EC2 service, you can add details like the tenancy, the operating system, the number of instances, instance type, payment options, volumes, and other information.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=145)** Once saved, you will see the estimated monthly cost.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=149)** As you can see, this tool can be handy for planning purposes.
>
> **[2:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=154)** Back over here to the Billing and Cost Management Console, let's look at Cost Explorer.
>
> **[2:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=160)** Here, I can see my total cost for the current and last 13 months, average monthly cost, count of services used and monthly graphs for cost.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=170)** Scroll down to see a monthly breakdown by service.
>
> **[2:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=174)** You can use filters to drill down such as the date range, granularity, service, account, region, and more.
>
> **[3:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=183)** You can also use cost allocation tags to filter.
>
> **[3:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=186)** For example, I'll filter by a user-defined cost allocation tag called cost center.
>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=193)** I'll apply the required tags and then click "Apply" and the graph reloads based on the chosen tags.
>
> **[3:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=201)** You can save these reports to access them later.
>
> **[3:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=204)** You can also create budgets from here.
>
> **[3:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=208)** When creating a budget, you can use templates such as zero spend or monthly cost budget or create a custom budget.
>
> **[3:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=217)** You can also add email addresses that should be notified when usage exceeds the budget.
>
> **[3:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=224)** I created a budget earlier to notify if the monthly usage goes above $50.
>
> **[3:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=230)** My current and forecasted usage is within the budget.
>
> **[3:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=234)** Under history, we can see monthly actual costs compared to the budgeted amount.
>
> **[4:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=240)** You can configure cost allocation tags from here.
>
> **[4:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=244)** The list of user-defined tags is populated from the tags you apply to your resources.
>
> **[4:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=250)** Select and activate the desired tags to include them in your cost and usage calculations.
>
> **[4:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=257)** The same goes for AWS-generated tags.
>
> **[4:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=259)** These are populated based on tags AWS applies to your resources.
>
> **[4:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=264)** You must also activate these if you want to include them in your reports.
>
> **[4:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=268)** You can create cost and usage reports from here.
>
> **[4:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=272)** AWS has a message that this page will be deprecated and move to data exports, which you will also find on the left navigation pane.
>
> **[4:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=281)** From here, you can create a report and deliver it to an S3 bucket.
>
> **[4:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=287)** The report will contain details of services and resources used and the cost allocation tags applied to them.
>
> **[4:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=294)** Lastly, to show you consolidated billing, I'll take you to the Billing and Cost Management Console of another AWS account.
>
> **[5:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=302)** I'm here at the Billing and Cost Management Console of another AWS account to show you consolidated billing.
>
> **[5:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=308)** I'm in the bills section and here, I have a summarized bill for all member accounts.
>
> **[5:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=314)** Scrolling down, I can view charges by account and then see a breakdown by service.
>
> **[5:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=323)** AWS enables consolidated billing when you create an AWS Organization.
>
> **[5:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=329)** All right.
>
> **[5:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=329)** So those are the tools to estimate project costs, find opportunities to reduce spending, and stay within budget.
>
> **[5:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/aws-essential-training-for-architects-23744949/tools-to-track-cost-and-usage?u=76281980&t=336)** Using these tools can help you make data-driven decisions to optimize costs.
